   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">International Women's Day</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div>

       Holiday to recognize women worldwide
      </div>

        <tr>
         <td class="sidebar-below"> <a href="/wiki/File:Woman-power_emblem.svg" class="image"><img alt="Woman-power emblem.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Woman-power_emblem.svg/17px-Woman-power_emblem.svg.png" decoding="async" width="17" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Woman-power_emblem.svg/26px-Woman-power_emblem.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Woman-power_emblem.svg/34px-Woman-power_emblem.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="648" data-file-height="1048"></a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Portal:Feminism" title="Portal:Feminism">Feminism portal</a></td>
        </tr>
        <tr>
         <td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style>
          <div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini">
           <ul>
            <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Feminism_sidebar" title="Template:Feminism sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Feminism_sidebar" title="Template talk:Feminism sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Feminism_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
           </ul>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p><b>International Women's Day</b> (<b>IWD</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Holiday" title="Holiday">global holiday</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_minor_secular_observances#March" title="List of minor secular observances">celebrated</a> annually on March 8 to commemorate the cultural, political, and socioeconomic achievements of women.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-4">[3]</a></sup> It is also a focal point in the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">women's rights movement</a>, bringing attention to issues such as <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_rights" title="Reproductive rights">reproductive rights</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women" title="Violence against women">violence against women</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>IWD originated from labor movements in North America and Europe during the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> The earliest version was purportedly a "Women's Day" organized by the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_America" title="Socialist Party of America">Socialist Party of America</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> February 28, 1909. This inspired German delegates at the <a href="/wiki/International_Socialist_Women%27s_Conferences" title="International Socialist Women's Conferences">1910 International Socialist Woman's Conference</a> to propose "a special Women's Day" be organized annually, albeit with no set date;<sup id="cite_ref-ICSW_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICSW-8">[7]</a></sup> the following year saw the first demonstrations and commemorations of International Women's Day across Europe. After women gained suffrage in <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Russia">Soviet Russia</a> in 1917 (the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a>), IWD was made a national <a href="/wiki/Holiday" title="Holiday">holiday</a> on March 8;<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> it was subsequently celebrated on that date by the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist movement">socialist movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communist_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist countries">communist countries</a>. The holiday was associated with far-left movements and governments until its adoption by the <a href="/wiki/Feminist_movement" title="Feminist movement">global feminist movement</a> in the late 1960s. IWD became a mainstream global holiday following its adoption by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>International Women's Day is commemorated in a variety of ways worldwide; it is a public holiday in several countries, and observed socially or locally in others.<sup id="cite_ref-RFE100_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFE100-11">[10]</a></sup> The UN observes the holiday in connection with a particular issue, campaign, or theme in women's rights.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> In some parts of the world, IWD still reflects its political origins, being marked by protests and calls for radical change; in other areas, particularly in the West, it is largely sociocultural and centered on a celebration of womanhood.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Zetkin_luxemburg1910.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Zetkin_luxemburg1910.jpg/220px-Zetkin_luxemburg1910.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Zetkin_luxemburg1910.jpg/330px-Zetkin_luxemburg1910.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Zetkin_luxemburg1910.jpg/440px-Zetkin_luxemburg1910.jpg 2x" data-file-width="872" data-file-height="1232"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Zetkin_luxemburg1910.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Clara_Zetkin" title="Clara Zetkin">Clara Zetkin</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Luxemburg" title="Rosa Luxemburg">Rosa Luxemburg</a> (right) in January 1910
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:N%C5%91nap_-_Petrogr%C3%A1d,_1917.03.08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/N%C5%91nap_-_Petrogr%C3%A1d%2C_1917.03.08.jpg/220px-N%C5%91nap_-_Petrogr%C3%A1d%2C_1917.03.08.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/N%C5%91nap_-_Petrogr%C3%A1d%2C_1917.03.08.jpg/330px-N%C5%91nap_-_Petrogr%C3%A1d%2C_1917.03.08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/N%C5%91nap_-_Petrogr%C3%A1d%2C_1917.03.08.jpg/440px-N%C5%91nap_-_Petrogr%C3%A1d%2C_1917.03.08.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:N%C5%91nap_-_Petrogr%C3%A1d,_1917.03.08.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Women's demonstration for bread and peace, Petrograd, Russia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:7_Demands_(1974).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/7_Demands_%281974%29.jpg/220px-7_Demands_%281974%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/7_Demands_%281974%29.jpg/330px-7_Demands_%281974%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/7_Demands_%281974%29.jpg/440px-7_Demands_%281974%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1269"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:7_Demands_(1974).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>British poster for Women's Day March, 1974
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The earliest purported Women's Day observance, called "<a href="/wiki/National_Woman%27s_Day" title="National Woman's Day">National Woman's Day</a>",<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> was held on February 28, 1909, in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, organized by the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_America" title="Socialist Party of America">Socialist Party of America</a><sup id="cite_ref-unevents_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unevents-15">[14]</a></sup> at the suggestion of activist <a href="/wiki/Theresa_Malkiel" title="Theresa Malkiel">Theresa Malkiel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> There have been claims that the day was commemorating a protest by women garment workers in New York on March 8, 1857, but researchers have alleged this to be a myth intended to detach International Women's Day from its socialist origin.<sup id="cite_ref-kaplan_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-17">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Françoise_Picq_1982_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Françoise_Picq_1982-18">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In August 1910, an <a href="/wiki/International_Socialist_Women%27s_Conferences#Copenhagen_1910" title="International Socialist Women's Conferences">International Socialist Women's Conference</a> was organized ahead of the general meeting of the Socialist <a href="/wiki/Second_International" title="Second International">Second International</a> in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ruthchild_2012_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ruthchild_2012-20">[19]</a></sup> Inspired in part by the American socialists, German delegates <a href="/wiki/Clara_Zetkin" title="Clara Zetkin">Clara Zetkin</a>, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A4te_Duncker" title="Käte Duncker">Käte Duncker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paula_Thiede" title="Paula Thiede">Paula Thiede</a>, and others proposed the establishment of an annual "Women's Day", although no date was specified.<sup id="cite_ref-ICSW_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICSW-8">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kaplan_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-17">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> The 100 delegates, representing 17 countries, agreed with the idea as a strategy to promote equal rights, including <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">women's suffrage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iwd_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iwd-22">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The following year, on March 19, 1911, the first International Women's Day (IWD) was marked by over a million people in Austria, Denmark, Germany, and Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-unevents_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unevents-15">[14]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> alone, there were 300 demonstrations,<sup id="cite_ref-kaplan_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-17">[16]</a></sup> with women parading on the <a href="/wiki/Ringstrasse" class="mw-redirect" title="Ringstrasse">Ringstrasse</a> in Vienna, carrying banners honoring the martyrs of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Commune" title="Paris Commune">Paris Commune</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kaplan_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-17">[16]</a></sup> Across Europe, women demanded the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_vote" class="mw-redirect" title="Right to vote">right to vote</a> and to hold public office, and protested against employment sex discrimination.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-4">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>IWD initially had no set date, though it was generally celebrated in late February or early March. Americans continued to observe "National Women's Day" on the last Sunday in February, while Russia observed International Women's Day for the first time in 1913, on the last Saturday in February (albeit based on the <a href="/wiki/Julian_calendar" title="Julian calendar">Julian calendar</a>, as in the Gregorian calendar, the date was March 8).<sup id="cite_ref-mmf1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmf1-23">[22]</a></sup> In 1914, International Women's Day was held on March 8 for the first time in Germany, possibly because that date was a Sunday.<sup id="cite_ref-mmf1_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmf1-23">[22]</a></sup> As elsewhere, Germany's observance was dedicated to women's right to vote, which German women did not win until 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-mmf1_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmf1-23">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> Concurrently, there was a march in London in support of women's suffrage, during which <a href="/wiki/Sylvia_Pankhurst" title="Sylvia Pankhurst">Sylvia Pankhurst</a> was arrested in front of <a href="/wiki/Charing_Cross" title="Charing Cross">Charing Cross</a> station on her way to speak in Trafalgar Square.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adoption_by_socialist_and_communist_movements">Adoption by socialist and communist movements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Adoption by socialist and communist movements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_of_USSR_1368.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Stamp_of_USSR_1368.jpg/200px-Stamp_of_USSR_1368.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="284" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Stamp_of_USSR_1368.jpg/300px-Stamp_of_USSR_1368.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Stamp_of_USSR_1368.jpg/400px-Stamp_of_USSR_1368.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1276" data-file-height="1809"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:1947_CPA_1140_cancelled.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/1947_CPA_1140_cancelled.jpg/200px-1947_CPA_1140_cancelled.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="284" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/1947_CPA_1140_cancelled.jpg/300px-1947_CPA_1140_cancelled.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/1947_CPA_1140_cancelled.jpg 2x" data-file-width="368" data-file-height="522"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          Soviet postage stamps
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On March 8, 1917 in <a href="/wiki/Petrograd" class="mw-redirect" title="Petrograd">Petrograd</a>, women textile workers began a demonstration that eventually engulfed the whole city, demanding "Bread and Peace"—an end to World War I, to food shortages, and to czarism.<sup id="cite_ref-mmf1_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmf1-23">[22]</a></sup> This marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a>, which alongside the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a>, made up the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-4">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> Revolutionary leader <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Leon Trotsky</a> wrote, "23 February (8th March) was International Woman's Day and meetings and actions were foreseen. But we did not imagine that this 'Women's Day' would inaugurate the revolution. Revolutionary actions were foreseen but without a date. But in the morning, despite the orders to the contrary, textile workers left their work in several factories and sent delegates to ask for the support of the strike… which led to mass strike... all went out into the streets."<sup id="cite_ref-mmf1_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmf1-23">[22]</a></sup> Seven days later, Tsar <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicholas II">Nicholas II</a> abdicated, and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government" title="Russian Provisional Government">provisional Government</a> granted women the right to vote.<sup id="cite_ref-unevents_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unevents-15">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1917, following the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolsheviks</a> <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_Kollontai" title="Alexandra Kollontai">Alexandra Kollontai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> made IWD an <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">official holiday</a> in the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> On May 8, 1965, the <a href="/wiki/USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="USSR">USSR</a> <a href="/wiki/Presidium_of_the_Supreme_Soviet" title="Presidium of the Supreme Soviet">Presidium of the Supreme Soviet</a> decreed International Women's Day a non-working day in the USSR, "in commemoration of the outstanding merits of Soviet women in communistic construction, in the defense of their Fatherland during the Great Patriotic War, in their heroism and selflessness at the front and in the rear, and also marking the great contribution of women to strengthening friendship between peoples, and the struggle for peace. But still, women's day must be celebrated as are other holidays."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>After its official adoption in Soviet Russia, IWD was predominantly celebrated in communist countries and by the communist movement worldwide. Communist leader <a href="/wiki/Dolores_Ib%C3%A1rruri" title="Dolores Ibárruri">Dolores Ibárruri</a> led a women's march in Madrid in 1936 on the eve of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kaplan_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-17">[16]</a></sup> Chinese communists observed the holiday beginning in 1922,<sup id="cite_ref-kaplan_17-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-17">[16]</a></sup> though it soon gained traction across the political spectrum: In 1927, <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a> saw a march of 25,000 women and male supporters, including representatives of the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a>, the <a href="/wiki/YWCA" title="YWCA">YWCA</a>, and labor organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> After the founding of the People's Republic of China on October 1, 1949, the State Council proclaimed on December 23 that March 8 would be made an official holiday, with women given a half-day off.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Worldwide_observance">Worldwide observance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Worldwide observance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Women%E2%80%99s_Day_March_(1975).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Women%E2%80%99s_Day_March_%281975%29.jpg/220px-Women%E2%80%99s_Day_March_%281975%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Women%E2%80%99s_Day_March_%281975%29.jpg/330px-Women%E2%80%99s_Day_March_%281975%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Women%E2%80%99s_Day_March_%281975%29.jpg/440px-Women%E2%80%99s_Day_March_%281975%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2642"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Women%E2%80%99s_Day_March_(1975).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Poster for Women's Day March in London, 1975
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>IWD remained predominantly a communist holiday until roughly 1967 when it was taken up by <a href="/wiki/Second-wave_feminism" title="Second-wave feminism">second-wave feminists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kaplan_17-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-17">[16]</a></sup> The day re-emerged as a day of activism, and is sometimes known in Europe as the "Women's International Day of Struggle". In the 1970s and 1980s, women's groups were joined by leftists and labor organizations in calling for equal pay, equal economic opportunity, equal legal rights, reproductive rights, subsidized child care, and the prevention of violence against women.<sup id="cite_ref-Søland_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Søland-30">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> began celebrating International Women's Day in 1975, which had been proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/International_Women%27s_Year" title="International Women's Year">International Women's Year</a>. In 1977, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> invited member states to proclaim March 8 as <a href="/wiki/UN_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Day">an official UN holiday</a> for <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">women's rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_peace" title="World peace">world peace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> It has since been commemorated annually by the UN and much of the world, with each year's observance centered on a particular theme or issue within women's rights. </p>
      <p>International Women's Day sparked violence in <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a>, Iran on March 4, 2007, when police beat hundreds of men and women who were planning a rally. (A previous rally for the occasion was held in Tehran in 2003.)<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> Police arrested dozens of women and some were released after several days of solitary confinement and interrogation.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shadi_Sadr" title="Shadi Sadr">Shadi Sadr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahbubeh_Abbasgholizadeh" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahbubeh Abbasgholizadeh">Mahbubeh Abbasgholizadeh</a> and several more community activists were released on March 19, 2007, ending a fifteen-day hunger strike.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By the twenty-first century, IWD has been criticized as heavily diluted and commercialized, particularly in the West, where it is sponsored by major corporations and used to promote general and vague notions of equality, rather than radical social reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-Blau_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blau-36">[35]</a></sup> In 2009, the British marketing firm Aurora Ventures set up a "International Women's Day" website with corporate sponsorship.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> The website began to promote hashtags as themes for the day, which became used internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> The day was commemorated by business breakfasts and social media communications that were deemed by some social critics as reminiscent of Mother's Day greetings.<sup id="cite_ref-Blau_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blau-36">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Søland_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Søland-30">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Yearly_commemorations">Yearly commemorations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Yearly commemorations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2010">IWD 2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: IWD 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GedWomenDay.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/GedWomenDay.JPG/220px-GedWomenDay.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/GedWomenDay.JPG/330px-GedWomenDay.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/GedWomenDay.JPG/440px-GedWomenDay.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GedWomenDay.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Women on the street celebrating International Women's Day in <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2018ko_martxoak_8,_greba_feminista_Iru%C3%B1ean_-_Goizeko_irudiak_18.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/2018ko_martxoak_8%2C_greba_feminista_Iru%C3%B1ean_-_Goizeko_irudiak_18.jpg/220px-2018ko_martxoak_8%2C_greba_feminista_Iru%C3%B1ean_-_Goizeko_irudiak_18.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/2018ko_martxoak_8%2C_greba_feminista_Iru%C3%B1ean_-_Goizeko_irudiak_18.jpg/330px-2018ko_martxoak_8%2C_greba_feminista_Iru%C3%B1ean_-_Goizeko_irudiak_18.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/2018ko_martxoak_8%2C_greba_feminista_Iru%C3%B1ean_-_Goizeko_irudiak_18.jpg/440px-2018ko_martxoak_8%2C_greba_feminista_Iru%C3%B1ean_-_Goizeko_irudiak_18.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="687"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2018ko_martxoak_8,_greba_feminista_Iru%C3%B1ean_-_Goizeko_irudiak_18.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>8M 2018 in <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On the occasion of 2010 International Women's Day the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">International Committee of the Red Cross</a> (ICRC) drew attention to the hardships displaced women endure. The displacement of populations is one of the gravest consequences of today's armed conflicts. It affects women in a host of ways.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2011">IWD 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: IWD 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Though the celebration in the West was low-key, events took place in more than 100 countries<sup id="cite_ref-RFE100_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFE100-11">[10]</a></sup> on March 8, 2011, to commemorate the 100th anniversary of International Women's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-DT100_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DT100-41">[40]</a></sup> In the United States, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> proclaimed March 2011 to be "<a href="/wiki/Women%27s_History_Month" title="Women's History Month">Women's History Month</a>", calling Americans to mark IWD by reflecting on "the extraordinary accomplishments of women" in shaping the country's history.<sup id="cite_ref-RFE100_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFE100-11">[10]</a></sup> Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> launched the "100 Women Initiative: Empowering Women and Girls through International Exchanges", on the eve of IWD.<sup id="cite_ref-VOA100_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOA100-42">[41]</a></sup> In the run-up to 2011 International Women's Day, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> called on States and other entities not to relent in their efforts to prevent rape and other forms of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a> that harm the lives and dignity of countless women in conflict zones around the world every year.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia issued an IWD 100th anniversary <a href="/wiki/Commemorative_coins_of_Australia#20_cent_coin" title="Commemorative coins of Australia">commemorative 20-cent coin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Egypt, in <a href="/wiki/Tahrir_Square" title="Tahrir Square">Tahrir Square</a>, Cairo, hundreds of men came out not to support, but to harass the women who came out to stand up for their rights as the police and military stood by watching, doing nothing to stop the crowds of men.<sup id="cite_ref-washpost-08-mar-14_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washpost-08-mar-14-45">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2012">IWD 2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: IWD 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a> America invited people to celebrate inspiring women in their lives by sending a free International Women's Day e-Card or honoring a woman whose efforts had made a difference in the fight against hunger and poverty with Oxfam's International Women's Day award.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On the occasion of International Women's Day 2012, the <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_of_the_Red_Cross" title="International Committee of the Red Cross">ICRC</a> called for more action to help the mothers and wives of people who have gone missing during armed conflict. The vast majority of people who go missing in connection with conflict are men. As well as the anguish of not knowing what has happened to the missing husband or son, many of these women face economic and practical difficulties. The ICRC underlined the duty of parties to this conflict to search for the missing and provide information to the families.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2013">IWD 2013</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: IWD 2013">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The International Committee of the Red Cross (ICRC) drew attention to the plight of women in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The theme for International Women's Day 2013 was "A promise is a promise: time for action to end violence against women."<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It was reported the 70% of women worldwide experience some sort of physical and/or sexual violence in their life. Irina Bovoka, UNESCO Director General on International Women's day 2013, stated that in order "to empower women and ensure equality, we must challenge every form of violence every time it occurs."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> In view of the increase in violence against women and following the brutal attack on Malala Yousafzai in October 2012, the UN focussed their attention on ending violence against women and made this the central theme for International Women's Day 2013. UNESCO acknowledged that violence against young girls was one of the major reasons for girls not attending school and subsequently collaborated with governments around the globe to support women's rights in providing a quality education in a safe environment. <sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For a more cultural and artistic celebration, UNESCO also held a concert in Paris as a "Tribute to Women in Music: from the romantic to the electronics". <sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2014">IWD 2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: IWD 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>American singer <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a> also posted an International Women's Day video to her YouTube account. Throughout the video, her song "<a href="/wiki/Flawless_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Flawless (Beyoncé song)">Flawless</a>" plays, which includes a portion of the "<a href="/wiki/We_Should_All_Be_Feminists" title="We Should All Be Feminists">We Should All Be Feminists</a>" speech given by author <a href="/wiki/Chimamanda_Ngozi_Adichie" title="Chimamanda Ngozi Adichie">Chimamanda Ngozi Adichie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2015">IWD 2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: IWD 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Governments and activists around the world commemorated the 20th anniversary year of the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Declaration" title="Beijing Declaration">Beijing Declaration</a> and Platform for Action, an historic roadmap that set the agenda for realizing <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">women's rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2016">IWD 2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: IWD 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The President of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pranab_Mukherjee" title="Pranab Mukherjee">Shri Pranab Mukherjee</a>, said: "On the occasion of International Women's Day, I extend warm greetings and good wishes to the women of India and thank them for their contributions over the years in the building of our nation."<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> The ministry of women and child development announced the setting up of four more one-stop crisis centers on March 8, in addition to the eight already functioning across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> Ahead of Women's Day, the national carrier Air India operated what it claimed to be the world's longest non-stop flight where the entire flight operations were handled by women, as part of International Women's Day celebrations. The flight, from Delhi to San Francisco, covered a distance of around 14,500 kilometers in around 17 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2017">IWD 2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: IWD 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In a message in support of International Women's Day, the UN Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="António Guterres">António Guterres</a> commented on how <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">women's rights</a> were being "reduced, restricted and reversed". With men still in leadership positions and a widening economic <a href="/wiki/Gender_pay_gap" title="Gender pay gap">gender gap</a>, he called for change "by empowering women at all levels, enabling their voices to be heard and giving them control over their own lives and over the future of our world".<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2018">IWD 2018</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: IWD 2018">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The UN theme for International Women's Day was: "Time is Now: Rural and urban activists transforming women’s lives”. </p>
      <p>Global marches and online campaigns such as #MeToo and #TimesUp, which originated in the United States but became popular globally, allowed many women from different parts of the world to confront injustice and speak out on issues such as sexual harassment and assault and the gender pay gap.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2019">IWD 2019</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: IWD 2019">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Concentraci%C3%B3n_del_Sindicato_de_Estudiantes_por_la_Huelga_Feminista_8M_2019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Concentraci%C3%B3n_del_Sindicato_de_Estudiantes_por_la_Huelga_Feminista_8M_2019.jpg/220px-Concentraci%C3%B3n_del_Sindicato_de_Estudiantes_por_la_Huelga_Feminista_8M_2019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Concentraci%C3%B3n_del_Sindicato_de_Estudiantes_por_la_Huelga_Feminista_8M_2019.jpg/330px-Concentraci%C3%B3n_del_Sindicato_de_Estudiantes_por_la_Huelga_Feminista_8M_2019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Concentraci%C3%B3n_del_Sindicato_de_Estudiantes_por_la_Huelga_Feminista_8M_2019.jpg/440px-Concentraci%C3%B3n_del_Sindicato_de_Estudiantes_por_la_Huelga_Feminista_8M_2019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Concentraci%C3%B3n_del_Sindicato_de_Estudiantes_por_la_Huelga_Feminista_8M_2019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>8M 2019 in Spain
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UN theme for International Women's Day was: 'Think equal, build smart, innovate for change'. The focus of the theme was on innovative ways in which to advance gender equality and the <a href="/wiki/Empowerment" title="Empowerment">empowerment</a> of women, particularly in the areas of <a href="/wiki/Social_protection" title="Social protection">social protection</a> systems, access to public services and <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_infrastructure" class="mw-redirect" title="Sustainable infrastructure">sustainable infrastructure</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The federal state of Berlin marked International Women's Day as a public holiday for the first time. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2020">IWD 2020</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: IWD 2020">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Reivindicaciones_8M_(49638492866).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Reivindicaciones_8M_%2849638492866%29.jpg/220px-Reivindicaciones_8M_%2849638492866%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Reivindicaciones_8M_%2849638492866%29.jpg/330px-Reivindicaciones_8M_%2849638492866%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Reivindicaciones_8M_%2849638492866%29.jpg/440px-Reivindicaciones_8M_%2849638492866%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1324" data-file-height="668"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Reivindicaciones_8M_(49638492866).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>8M 2020 in Spain
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The UN theme for International Women's Day was: 'I am Generation Equality': Realizing Women's Rights'.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> Despite the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, street marches occurred in London, Paris, Madrid, Brussels, Moscow and other European cities.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-62">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Aurat_March#2020_protests" title="Aurat March">Aurat March</a> in <a href="/wiki/Islamabad" title="Islamabad">Islamabad</a> was marred by attacks from stone throwers, after a failed attempt to have it banned as un-<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a>, the capital of <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>, police detained dozens of marchers shortly after masked men reportedly attacked the march.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-62">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table role="presentation" class="mbox-small-left plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IWD_2021">IWD 2021</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: IWD 2021">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The 2021 UN theme for International Women's Day is "Women in leadership: Achieving an equal future in a COVID-19 world", highlighting the impact that girls and women worldwide had as health care workers, caregivers, innovators and community organizers during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> The theme this year is: #ChooseToChallenge. </p> 
      <table role="presentation" class="mbox-small-left plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Wikimedia-logo.svg/40px-Wikimedia-logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Wikimedia-logo.svg/60px-Wikimedia-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Wikimedia-logo.svg/80px-Wikimedia-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="1024"></td> 
         <td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikispore has a related page: <i><b><a href="https://wikispore.wmflabs.org/wiki/Event:International_Women%27s_Day_2021" class="extiw" title="wikispore:Event:International Women's Day 2021">Event:International Women's Day 2021</a></b></i></td>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Around_the_world">Around the world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Around the world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:International_Women%27s_Day_celebration.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/International_Women%27s_Day_celebration.png/260px-International_Women%27s_Day_celebration.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/International_Women%27s_Day_celebration.png/390px-International_Women%27s_Day_celebration.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/International_Women%27s_Day_celebration.png/520px-International_Women%27s_Day_celebration.png 2x" data-file-width="1978" data-file-height="1004"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:International_Women%27s_Day_celebration.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:red; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Official holiday
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:orange; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Holiday for women
         </div> 
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
         <div class="legend">
          <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:yellow; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Non-official holiday
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>IWD is an official holiday in several countries worldwide, including Afghanistan,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> Angola, Armenia,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> Azerbaijan,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> Belarus,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> Burkina Faso,<sup id="cite_ref-capacity4dev_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-capacity4dev-72">[71]</a></sup> Cambodia,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> China (for women only),<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> Cuba,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> Georgia,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> Germany (Berlin only),<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> Guinea-Bissau, Eritrea, Kazakhstan,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> Kyrgyzstan,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> Laos,<sup id="cite_ref-laoyp_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laoyp-80">[79]</a></sup> Madagascar (for women only),<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> Moldova,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> Mongolia,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> Nepal, Russia, Tajikistan, Turkmenistan, Uganda, Ukraine,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> Uzbekistan,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> and Zambia.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mimosa2007.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mimosa2007.JPG/220px-Mimosa2007.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mimosa2007.JPG/330px-Mimosa2007.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Mimosa2007.JPG/440px-Mimosa2007.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mimosa2007.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Acacia_dealbata" title="Acacia dealbata">Yellow mimosa</a> is the symbol of IWD in <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and Italy
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In some countries, such as Australia,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> Cameroon,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> Croatia,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> Romania,<sup id="cite_ref-agentia.org_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agentia.org-90">[89]</a></sup> Bosnia and Herzegovina,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> Bulgaria,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> Vietnam,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> and Chile;<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> IWD is not an official public holiday, but is widely observed nonetheless. </p>
      <p>Regardless of legal status, in much of the world, it is customary for men to give female colleagues and loved ones flowers and small gifts. In some countries (such as Bulgaria and Romania) it is also observed as an equivalent of Mother's Day, where children also give small presents to their mothers and grandmothers.<sup id="cite_ref-agentia.org_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agentia.org-90">[89]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic" title="Czechoslovak Socialist Republic">Czechoslovak Socialist Republic</a>, huge Soviet-style celebrations were held annually. After the fall of Communism, the holiday, generally considered to be one of the major symbols of the old regime, fell into obscurity. International Women's Day was re-established as an official "important day" by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Parliament of the Czech Republic">Parliament of the Czech Republic</a> in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-Kapusta‐Pofahl_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kapusta‐Pofahl-95">[94]</a></sup> on the proposal of the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Social_Democratic_Party" title="Czech Social Democratic Party">Social Democrats</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia" title="Communist Party of Bohemia and Moravia">Communists</a>. This has provoked some controversy as a large part of the public as well as the political right see the holiday as a relic of the nation's Communist past.<sup id="cite_ref-Kapusta‐Pofahl_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kapusta‐Pofahl-95">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>IWD is widely celebrated in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> as <a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Journ%C3%A9e_internationale_des_femmes" class="extiw" title="fr:Journée internationale des femmes">Journée internationale des femmes</a>. In Italy, the holiday is observed by men giving <a href="/wiki/Acacia_dealbata" title="Acacia dealbata">yellow mimosas</a> to women.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> This originated with communist politician <a href="/wiki/Teresa_Mattei" title="Teresa Mattei">Teresa Mattei</a>, who chose the mimosa in 1946 as the symbol of IWD because the predominant symbols of the day, <a href="/wiki/Violet_(plant)" class="mw-redirect" title="Violet (plant)">violets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lily-of-the-valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Lily-of-the-valley">lily-of-the-valley</a>, were too scarce and expensive to be used effectively in Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-florentine_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-florentine-98">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the United States, actress and human rights activist <a href="/wiki/Beata_Pozniak" class="mw-redirect" title="Beata Pozniak">Beata Pozniak</a> worked with the Mayor of Los Angeles and the Governor of California to lobby members of the US Congress to propose official recognition of the holiday. In February 1994, by <a href="/wiki/Beata_Pozniak" class="mw-redirect" title="Beata Pozniak">Beata Pozniak</a> suggestion, the H. J. Res. 316 was introduced by Representative <a href="/wiki/Maxine_Waters" title="Maxine Waters">Maxine Waters</a>, along with 79 cosponsors, in an attempt to officially recognize March 8 of that year as International Women's Day. The bill was subsequently referred to, and remained in, the House Committee on Post Office and Civil Service. No vote of either house of Congress was achieved on this piece of legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-billsummary_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billsummary-99">[98]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Aurat_March" title="Aurat March">Aurat March</a> has challenged misogyny since 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_UN_themes">Official UN themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Official UN themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Women%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">English&nbsp;: "Give Us Women's Suffrage. Women's Day, March 8, 1914. Until now, prejudice and reactionary attitudes have denied full <a href="/wiki/Civic_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Civic rights">civic rights</a> to women, who as workers, mothers, and citizens wholly fulfill their duty, who must pay their taxes to the state as well as the municipality. Fighting for this natural human right must be the firm, unwavering intention of every woman, every female worker. In this, no pause for rest, no respite is allowed. Come all, you women and girls, to the 9th public women's assembly on Sunday, March 8, 1914, at 3&nbsp;pm."<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
